Jamison Brereton

128
Agni
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
8 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi
The sacrificial fire is the relentless focus of this hymn, and it seldom strays from the physical location of the fire on the ritual ground. Though its theme is clear and inescapable, the hymn presents us with manifold interpretive difficulties in its details, especially in the central verses 4тАУ5, which, with their responsive fronted kr├бtv─Б (тАЬthough his resolve,тАЭ 4cd, 5a), may constitute an omphalos. There is also some sign of ring composition: the first and last (8) verses each twice refer to Agni as the Hotar, a word used nowhere else in the hymn, and the mentions of Manu in verses 1тАУ2 are answered by two occurrences of Manu in the penultimate verse (7). In general there is much reuse of vocabulary through the hymn, and the poet plays with the words тАЬgoodтАЭ and тАЬgoodsтАЭ in the second part of the hymn (vss. 5тАУ6, 8). Though the poet does not himself beg for goods, it seems clear that the desire for goods he attributes to the gods (8fg) is shared by their human counterparts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Agni, the invoker of the gods, the assiduous offerer of sacrifices, is genitive rated of man, (for the fulfilment of the) duty of those who desire (the fruit of) pious rites as well as for (the discharge of) his own duty; he is the bestower of all blessings on him who desires his friendship, and is wealth to (such a one) seeking for food; the unobstructed offerer of oblations, he sits down, surrounded (by ministering priests), on the most sacred spot of earth upon the footmark of Iс╕╖a.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Niс╣гadad-iс╕╖aspade pariv─лta: niс╣гadad-iс╕╖aspade = bh┼лmy─Бha pade, on a spot or site of ground; dharimani (of previous hymn) = that spot which contains the essence of the earth, i.e. the altar. vedim─Бhuс╕е paramantam pс╣Ыthivy─Бс╕е = they call the altar the utmost end of the earth (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 7.4.18.2); et─Бvati vai pс╣Ыthiv─лr y─Бvat─л vediriti = so much, verily, as is the earth as much is the altar (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 1.1.4.4). pariv─лta iс╕╖aspade: the reference is to Iс╕╖─Б, daughter of Manu and pada = the spot where in the form a cow (gor┼лpa). she plural ced her feet; p─Бdany─Бsa prade┼Ыe = allusion to the legend of Manu’s daughter being the first instrumental tutor of sacrificial rites; iс╕╖a vai m─Бnav─л yaj├▒─Бn┼лk─Б┼Ыin y─Бs─лd it─лd─Бy─Б pade ghс╣Ыtavati sv─Бh─Б (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 1.2.5.1) = Ida, the daughter of Manu, was the instrumental tutor of sacrifice, glory to the butter charged footmark of Iс╕╖a

Jamison Brereton

This one was born here on the foundation of Manu as the best sacrificing Hotar, following the commandment of the fire-priestsтАФAgni,
following his own commandmentтАФ
all attentive to the one who seeks a comrade, like wealth for the one who seeks fame.
The undeceivable Hotar has sat down in the footprint of refreshmentтАФ enveloped in the footprint of refreshment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase m├бnuс╣гo dh├бr─лmaс╣Зi is variously rendered. Renou takes it as an infinitive (тАЬpour ├кtre port├й par lтАЩHommeтАЭ); Grassmann and Oldenberg (SBE) interpret it in an abstract or ethical fashion (тАЬnach altem BrauchтАЭ; тАЬin ManuтАЩs firm lawтАЭ; sim.

Brereton in his survey of dh├бrman-). Hoffmann (Inj. 121, fld by Witzel Got┼Н) as тАШhandsтАЩ. But given the emphasis in the verse on the activity on the ritual ground (bc) and indeed the fireтАЩs placement on said ground (fg), GeldnerтАЩs тАЬim (Feuer)beh├дlter des ManuтАЭ seems the most likely interpr. – rendered by me as тАЬthe foundation of Manu,тАЭ making reference to the fact that Manu was the first sacrificer and so every subsequent ritual ground can be ascribed to him. See 7a m─Б╠Бnuс╣гe vс╣Ыj├бne тАШin the ritual enclosure belonging to ManuтАЩ for another association between Manu and a physical location on the ritual ground.

As usual the line between human priests and Agni as priest is blurred in bc.

Agni is regularly identified as an u┼Ы├нj- (I.60.4, etc.) but u┼Ы├нjaс╕е in the plural are humans.

тАЬIn the footprint of refreshmentтАЭ (iс╕╖├бs pad├й) is a standard kenning for the ritual ground or, more narrowly, the place where oblations are offered; a similar expression is found in Oldenberg Avestan, at Y. 50.8.

Griffith

By Manu’s law was born this Agni, Priest most skilled, born for the holy work of those who yearn therefore, yea, born for his own holy work.
All ear to him who seeks his love and wealth to him who strives for fame,
Priest ne’er deceived, he sits in Ila’s holy place, girt round in Ila’s holy place.

Oldenberg

He was born in Manu’s firm law 1, the Hotri, the best sacrificer, according to the will of the Usigs 2, Agni, according to his own will. Always listening to him who wishes to be his friend, like a treasure to him who aspires to renown, the unbeguiled Hotri sat down in the abode of food (on the altar); enveloped 3 (he sat down) in the abode of food.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe propitiate that instrumental ument of sacrifice by the path of sacrifice, by reverential salutation, and by oblations of clarified butter; by oblations (offered) to the gods and he accepts our offerings, and through his benignity quits not (the rite until its close), the divinity whom the wind brought from afar for the service of Manu; (may he come) from afar (to our sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bh─Бс╕е par─Бvata-abh─Бs─лt, shone or made to shine, plural ced suitably upon earth, having been brought from the distant sun: atid┼лram gatavata ─Бdity─Бd abh─Бs─лt aucityena bh┼лmau sth─Бpitav─Бn

Jamison Brereton

The one who sends the sacrifice to its goal along the path of truth: we make him our familiar with reverence accompanied by oblationsтАФin the conclave of gods (with reverence) accompanied by oblations.
Because of our presentation of nourishments he does not waste away with this body,
he whom M─Бtari┼Ыvan (brought) to Manu from afarтАФthe god he brought from afar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of ├бpi тИЪvat roughly follows TichyтАЩs (Die Spr. 26 [1980]: 3-5, esp. n. 8 [= KlSch 108-10]) тАШmit etw. (Akk.) bekannt, vertaut seinтАЩ (contra ThiemeтАЩs Fs. Weller)тАФthough perhaps with a bit more oomph.

I construe с╣Ыt├бsya path─Б╠Бin b with yaj├▒as─Б╠Бdham in a, flg. L├╝ders (Var. 463) – contra most interpr., who take it as roughly parallel to the other instr. expressions in b. It is true that there is some distance between the two expressions I put together, and Geldner also cites two parallels where с╣Ыt├бsya path─Б╠Бis adjacent to n├бmas─Б. However, in both those instances the two instrumentals are better taken with different parts of the verse, and since L├╝dersтАЩs interpr. yields richer sense, I maintain it here.

Griffith

We call that perfecter of worship by the path or sacrifice; with reverence rich in offerings, with worship rich in offerings.
Through presentation of our food he grows not old in this his from;
The God whom Matarisvan brought from far away, for Manu brought from far away.

Oldenberg

We render him attentive 1, the promoter of sacrifice, on the path of Rita, by adoration with offerings, in the divine world, by (adoration) with offerings 2. In bringing us vigour he never becomes worn out with this body of his: he whom M├вtarisvan (has brought) to Manu from afar, the god whom he has brought from afar.

Durch unsere Darreichung von St├дrkungen altert er nicht in dieser Gestalt; er, den Matarisvan f├╝r Manu aus der Ferne brachte, der Gott, den er aus der Ferne brachte.

Wir regen an den Opfersegner auf dem Pfad des heil’gen Werks mit opferreicher Huldigung, mit opferreichem Gottesdienst, Durch unsrer Speisen Dargebot ist unverg├дnglich seine Pracht; Den Matari├зvan aus der Ferne hergebracht, dem Menschen hergebracht den Gott.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who is ever to be hymned, the giver of food, the showerer (of benefits), comes immediately (upon our invocation), in approach to (the altar of) earth, loud-sounding, vigorous, and loud-sounding; the rapid and divine (Agni, incited by praise), manifests himself a hundredfold by his flames; Agni, having his abode in high plural ce, (comes quickly) to pious rites.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

On his way he circles round the earthly (realm) in a single day,
swallowing it up in an instant, the bull (depositing) his seed ever
roaringтАФdepositing his seed ever roaringтАФ
observing with a hundred eyes, the god victorious in the woods,
taking his seat on the nearer ridgesтАФAgni, on the further ridges.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (as well as Scarlatta. 110-11) take -g├нr- in muhurg─л╠Бr to тИЪgс╣Э тАШsingтАЩ, rather than, with Grassmann, to тИЪgс╣Э тАШswallowтАЩ. This is certainly possible, though тАЬтАШpl├╢tzlich, augenblichlich willkommen geheissenтАЩ (?)тАЭ (Scarlatta 110; sim. Witzel Got┼Н) does not have much to do with what proceeds or follows in the verse. I prefer to keep GrassmannтАЩs тАШauf einmal verschlingendтАЩ. The expression completes the description of AgniтАЩs journey in the preceding p─Бda. The speed of his journey around the world, completed in a single day, is conveyed by the image of тАЬswallowing upтАЭ the route instantly – similar expressions are found in English. EWA (s.vv. GARI1 , GARI2 ) is uncertain of the root affiliation.

Griffith

In ordered course forthwith he traverses the earth, swift-swallowing, bellowing Steer, bearing the genial seed, bearing the seed and bellowing.
Observant with a hundred eyes the God is conqueror in the wood:
Agni, who hath his seat in broad plains here below, and in the high lands far away.

Oldenberg

In his (own) way he moves in one moment round the terrestrial (space), the sudden devourer (emitting) his sperm, the bellowing bull emitting his sperm, the bellower 1, looking round with a hundred eyes, the god who quickly courses in the forests 2, taking his seat on the lower ridges, Agni, and on the highest ridges.

Geldner

In raschem Lauf umkreist er in einem Tag den irdischen Raum, wiederholt die Stimme erhebend, ein Stier, der unter Br├╝llen Samen l├дsst, unter Br├╝llen Samen lassend; mit hundert Augen blickend, der Gott in den H├╢lzern siegreich, seinen Sitz in den unteren Erhebungen nehmend und in den h├╢chsten H├╢hen, der Agni.

Grassmann

Auf seinem Gang umwandelt t├дglich er die Welt, den Samen lassend br├╝llt mit hellem Schrei der Stier, den Samen lassend br├╝llt er laut; Mit hundert Augen schaut der Gott, der in den H├╢lzern Sieger ist; Den Sitz einnehmend in den untern R├дumen hier, und in den h├╢chsten Agni dort.

Elizarenkova

рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдЬрд╛рдпрдд рд╕рдорд░реНрдереЛрд╜рднрд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThat Agni, who is (the performer of) holy acts, the priest of the family, thinks in every dwelling of the imperishable sacrifice; he thinks of the sacrifice (reminded) by (its) celebration; for through such pious rite, he, the bestower of (fit) rewards, accepts all the offered oblations for (the good of) the worshipper, whence he has become as a guest, fed abundantly with butter; and the offere (of the oblations) has become the realizer of the rewards (of the worship).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Strongly resolved (to sacrifice), installed in front in every house, Agni is attentive to the sacrifice, to the ceremonyтАФthrough his resolve he is attentive to the sacrifice.
Through his resolve he is a ritual expert for the straight-arrow; he has watched over all beings
from the time when as guest he was born splendid with gheeтАФas the conveyor (of the offering), the ritual expert, he was born.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The part. iс╣г┼лy├бnt- in d is generally tr. тАШshooting arrowsтАЩ (though cf. RenouтАЩs тАЬqui cherche la jouissance-rituelleтАЭ; sim. Oldenberg SBE [but not Noten]), but shooting arrows seems out of place in this context, even with GeldnerтАЩs suggestion (n. 4d) that the priest is compared to a shooter because his words are arrows. Although I maintain the connection with тАШarrowтАЩ, I think it means simply тАШgo (straight) like an arrowтАЩ, readily translatable into the English idiom тАШstraight-arrowтАЩ, namely a person of utmost rectitude.

Griffith

That Agni, wise High-Priest, in every house takes thought for sacrifice and holy service, yea, takes thought, with mental power, for sacrifice.
Disposer, he with mental power shows all things unto him who strives;
Whence he was born a guest enriched with holy oil, born as Ordainer and as Priest.

Oldenberg

This highly wise Purohita, Agni watches sacrifice and service 1 house by house; by (the power of) his mind he is intent upon sacrifice. By (the power of) his mind helpful to him who desires food 2, he looks on all creatures, since he has been born, the guest adorned with ghee, (since) the helpful carrier (of the gods) 3 has been born.

Geldner

Agni, der Einsichtsvolle, der bevollm├дchtigte Priester in jedem Haus versteht sich auf Opfer und Gottesdienst; mit Umsicht versteht er sich auf das Opfer. Durch Umsicht versteht er sich auf das Opfer. Durch Umsicht ein vorbildlicher Meister f├╝r den, der den Pfeil schie├Яt, hat er acht auf alle Wesen, sobald er, der schmalzversch├╢nte Gast geboren ward, wenn der Opferlenker und Meister geboren ward.

Grassmann

Der weisheitsvolle Priester sorgt in jedem Haus f├╝r Opfers Feier Agni mit des Geistes Kraft, auf jedes Opfer achtet er; Er hilft mit Kraft dem strebenden und schaut auf alle Wesen hin, Seit der mit Butter reich versehne Gast erstand, der treue Opferer erstand.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as (all men) offer in holy rite (food) for his satisfaction in the blazing (flames) of Agni, like (the grains that) are to be enjoyed by the winds, and like the viands that are to be given to him who solicits them; therefore the worshipper presents gifts to him, according to the extent of his opulence; and he preserves us, when oppressed (by sin), from wickedness; from overpowering malevolence and sin.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When through his resolve and along with the roaring of fire, which is like the roaring of the Maruts [=thunder], the (offering-)foods are infused into his forces [=flames]тАФlike foods for the vigorous one [=Indra?]тАФ
because then he stimulates the giving (of good) and of goods by his might, he will rescue us from going astray, from the crooked wayтАФfrom evil utterance, from the crooked way.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A complex vs., esp. in its earlier parts, with a variety of tr. I will treat only my own. But first a few textual adjustments. In b I read (with most interpr., going back to Ludwig; see Oldenberg and GeldnerтАЩs n. 5b) agn├й r├бveс╣Зa rather than Pp. agn├йr ├бveс╣Зa.

Note also that the sandhi between b and c has been wrongly resolved by Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition into bhoj├нye / aтАж rather than bhoj├нy─Б / iтАж (here Pp. is correct). And the first word of c has the wrong sibilant in the Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition text: itтАЩs correctly iс╣гir─Б╠Бya, not i┼Ыir─Б╠Бya.

Also in b I take the simile as consisting only of mar├║t─Бс╣Г n├б rather than including bhojy─Б╠А. This genitive modifies r├бveс╣Зa and is parallel to agn├й(r). The roaring of Agni is being compared to the roaring of the Maruts, personifications of the thunderstorm. This syntactic distribution is found in Oldenberg SBE, but subsequent tr.

have not followed him.

I take the bhojy─Б╠Аas nominative and the subject of an intrans./passive use of med. pс╣Ы├▒c├бte, a usage found elsewhere. However, it is not impossible that this med.

form is transitive – cf. ─Б╠БтАж pс╣Ыc─лmahi in the next hymn (I.129.7) – in which case I would supply тАШpriestsтАЩ as subj.: тАЬ(The priests) infuse the (offering-)foods into his forces.тАЭ In p─Бda a I take t├бviс╣г─лс╣гu тАШforcesтАЩ as a reference to AgniтАЩs flames. Although t├бviс╣г─л- ordinarily belong to Indra, see, e.g., III.3.5, 26.4 for t├бviс╣г─лbhiс╕е in conjunction with Agni.

I tentatively take Indra as the referent for iс╣гir─Б╠Бya in c, as he is addressed as iс╣гira in the first vs. of the next hymn (I.129.1) and is several times the referent of this stem elsewhere. But I do not insist on this identification.

The ca in de is problematic, and this problem is connected with the question of the affiliation of v├бs┼лn─Бm. Geldner (fld. by Klein, DGRV I.234) takes ca as a clausal conjunction and supplies a 2nd verb тАЬ(beschenkt)тАЭ in d, parallel to ├нnvati in c. This requires that v├бs┼лn─Бm be construed with majm├бn─Б (тАЬmit einer F├╝lle von G├╝ternтАЭ).

But majm├бn─Б does not take a genitive of specification but only of possession and in any case its contexts favor тАШmightтАЩ over тАШabundanceтАЩ. Several times it appears parallel with kr├бtv─Б (including nearby I.141.6, 143.2) in the collocation тАЬwith resolve and with might,тАЭ as it would here, though at some remove (see kr├бtv─Б in p─Бda a).

Forms of v├бsu- regularly occur with forms of тИЪd─Б тАШgiveтАЩ, however, and so the most natural collocation here would be d─Б╠Бnam тАж v├бs┼лn─Бm тАЬthe giving of goods.тАЭ But what, then, to do with the ca? I think the clue is to be found in X.50.7 v├бs┼лn─Бс╣Г ca v├бsuna┼Ы ca d─Бv├бne тАЬfor the giving of goods and of goodтАЭ; in other words, I think the v├бs┼лn─Бс╣Г ca in our passage is a truncated formula, with v├бsuna┼Ы ca gapped. But the omitted sg. v├бsu- is immediately inserted in the first p─Бda of the next verse (6a) and the number-neutralized stem occurs three times in vs. 8: v├бsudhitim (8a), vas┼лy├бvaс╕е (8f, g). Note also that a different form of v├бsu appears to be gapped in 6ab. The poet slyly sets the v├бsu- agenda in 5de by introducing it with an off-balance expression that requires repair. For a similarly problematic ca involving (in my opinion) gapping, see the previous hymn, I.127.8 and disc. there.

The phrase ┼Ы├бс╣Гs─Бd agh─Б╠Бt corresponds to the well-attested bahuvr─лhi agh├б┼Ыaс╣Гsa- тАШpossessing evil speechтАЩ, found in the next hymn (I.129.6).

Griffith

When through his power and in his strong prevailing flames the Maruts’ gladdening boons mingle with Agni’s roar, boons gladdening for the active One,
Then he accelerates the gift, and by the greatness of his wealth,
Shall rescue us from overwhelming misery, from curse and overwhelming woe.

Oldenberg

When through his (Agni’s) power the bounties grow in strength, with the roar of Agni 1 as with that of the Maruts 2тАФlike bounties offered to a vigorous man: then he by his greatness stirs up the gift of goods. May he protect us from misfortune and injury, from evil spell and injury.

Geldner

Wenn sie mit Umsicht unter seine Kr├дfte die Opfergen├╝sse mischen bei Agni┬┤s Gebr├╝ll, wie die Gen├╝sse der Marut, wie die Gen├╝sse f├╝r den Eifrigen - Er f├╢rdert ja die Schenkung und beschenkt mit einer F├╝lle von G├╝tern. Er m├╢ge uns vor Mi├Яerfolg, vor R├дnken, vor dem b├╢sen Gerede des R├дnkes├╝chtigen bewahren.

Grassmann

Mit Agni’s Kraft und Lust bei seinem Ungest├╝m vermischen sich Gen├╝sse wie der Marutschar, Gen├╝sse f├╝r den munteren; Denn er beschleunigt das Geschenk der G├╝ter auch nach seiner Macht, Er m├╢g’ uns retten vor Gefahr und Ungl├╝cksfall, vor b├╢sem Fluch und Ungl├╝cksfall.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe universal mighty and imperious (Agni) holds riches in his right hand; but, like the sun, he loosens his grip (in favour of his worshipper), although he relaxes not from his desire of the (sacrificial) food. Verily, Agni, you bear the oblation to every one of the gods who desires it; Agni grants blessings to every pious (worshipper), and opens for him the gates (of heaven).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Arati = one who is not easily plural ased, a sovereign: aratir─л┼Ыvara aramam─Бnaс╕е v─Б apr─лt─л; taraс╣Зir na = t─Бrakaс╕е s┼лrya iva, like whom who conveys across (the sea of life or the world), i.e. the sun or Agni: na ┼Ыi┼Ыrathat, not loosened; i.e. the conveyor (across the world) has not deserted his worshipper

Jamison Brereton

Every (new fire), possessing extensive power, the spoked wheel (of the sacrifice), the good one, takes (goods) in his right hand; advancing he does not let (them) looseтАФbecause of his longing for fame he does not let (them) loose.
For everyone who aims straight you have conveyed his oblation among the gods.
To everyone who performs well he propels his wishтАФAgni propels apart the two door-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner, Renou, and Oldenberg I supply an acc. pl. v├бs┼л(ni) as obj. of dadhe, on the basis of IX.18.4 v├бs┼лni h├бstayor dadh├й (cf. also X.54.5). The gapping of a form of v├бsu- here, accepted by most, corresponds nicely to the gapping of the same stem I suggest for the previous vs. Thieme (Unters.), fld. by Witzel Got┼Н, instead take dadhe as passive: the fire тАЬis taken in the handтАЭ (of the priest, so Thieme). This seems pragmatically unlikely: although firebrands are ritually carried about under certain circumstances, picking up the entire ritual fire (as v├нh─Бy─Бс╕е and arat├нс╕е seem to imply) would be risky and painful. Moreover, the rest of the verse depicts the good things that Agni does for people, and taking goods in his hand fits this context.

The rarely attested verbal stem iс╣гudhy├б-, here in the part. iс╣гudhyat├й, has a counterpart in Oldenberg Avestan, i┼б┼лidii─Бmah─л 3x in the Yasna Hapta┼Лh─Бiti, which exists alongside a noun i┼бud-. The form is carefully discussed by Narten (YH 159-61), who accepts HumbachтАЩs etymology (Gathas 1959, II, ad Y 31.14; repeated 2nd ed. 1991): i┼бud- is a compound of i┼б- тАШnourishmentтАЩ and the zero-grade of *тИЪvadh тАШleadтАЩ, to which root noun compound a denom. is built meaning тАШstrengthenтАЩ. (For a rehearsal of the history of this scholarship, see Scarlatta 63.) I am not convinced. I prefer to see it (couched in Vedic terms for the moment) as a compound of ├нс╣гu- тАШarrowтАЩ and тИЪdh─Б тАШplaceтАЩ. That lexeme is specialized in the meaning тАШaimтАЩ and is a well-attested metaphor for the тАЬaimingтАЭ of a praise-hymn towards the divine recipient; cf. IX.69.1 ├нс╣гur n├б dh├бnvan pr├бti dh─лyate mat├нс╕е тАЬLike an arrow on a bow, my thought is aimed.тАЭ (For the affinity of ├нс╣гu- and тИЪdh─Б cf. also I.64.10 ├бst─Бra ├нс╣гuс╣Г dadhire g├бbhastayoс╕е тАЬThe archers have taken their arrows in their fistsтАЭ and the cmpd. iс╣гu-dh├н- тАШquiverтАЩ.) Such an analysis works also for the Avestan forms, since Avestan has both the тАШarrowтАЩ word and the verb, and I see no reason why it could not be reconstructed for Indo-Iranian. An тАШarrowтАЩ derivation works extremely well in our passage because iс╣гudhyat├й echoes iс╣г┼лyat├й (тАШgoing straight like an arrowтАЩ) in vs. 4, likewise ending the d-p─Бda, likewise a denominative participial dat. of benefit. For extensive and updated disc. see my forthcoming тАЬVedic iс╣гudhy├б- and Oldenberg Avestan i┼бud-, i┼б┼лidiia-: The Aim of Praise.тАЭ The 2nd person of pf. ├│hiс╣гe is puzzling in a verse, and a hymn, in which the god is otherwise entirely referred to in the 3rd ps. (see the surrounding verbs in this vs.: dadhe (a), ┼Ыi┼Ыrathat (bc), с╣Ыс╣Зvati (fg) – with p─Бda f esp. entirely parallel to de with 2nd ps. ├│hiс╣гe). I think it must be a transposition of the phrase found in VIII.19.1 devatr─Б╠Бhavy├бm ├│hire тАЬThey have carried the oblation among the gods.тАЭ The expected 3rd sg. pf. ├│he would not fit the meter here.

Though p─Бdas f and g share both a subject (Agni) and a verb (v├н) с╣Ыс╣Зvati they seem semantically somewhat at odds. This semantic disparity is, however, ameliorated by the fact that their objects, v─Б╠Бram and dv─Б╠Бr─Б respectively, are phonologically very close, which similarity was already pointed out by Renou

Griffith

Vast, universal, good he was made messenger; the speeder with his right hand hath not loosed his hold, through love of fame not loosed his hold.
He bears oblations to the Gods for whosoever supplicates.
Agni bestows a blessing on each pious man, and opens wide the doors for him.

Oldenberg

The far-reaching 1 steward 2 has taken all goods 3 in his right hand, and strongly advancing does not let them loose; desirous of glory he does not let them loose. For every supplicant 4 thou hast carried the oblations to the gods 5. For every righteous one he procures a treasure; Agni opens both folds of the door (for him).

Geldner

Ganz bei voller Kraft wird er der Wagenlenker, h├дlt der Gott die G├╝ter in seiner rechten Hand. Ausdauernd l├дsst er nicht locker, aus Ehrgeiz Opfer zu den G├╢ttern gefahren. Jedem Frommen erf├╝llt er den Wunsch, ├╢ffnet Agni die Tore.

Grassmann

Der grosse, gute Weltenopfrer ist gesetzt; nicht lass er los mit seiner Rechten, wenn er siegt, nicht lass er los voll Beutelust; Du f├дhrst das Opfer g├╢tterw├дrts f├╝r jeden eifrig strebenden, Ja, jedem Frommen schliesst er sch├╢ne Sch├дtze auf, die Th├╝ren schliesset Agni auf.

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрди рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ) рд╕рдордЧреНрд░ (рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд (рдЕрд░рддрд┐рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐ рдХрд░рд╛рддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рддрд░рдгрд┐рдГ) рддрд╛рд░рдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░рд╛ (рд╡рд╕реБрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдердо рд╢реНрд░реЗрдгреА рдХрд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдпрд╛) рдЕрдкрдиреА рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рд╕реБрдирдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рди (рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерддреН) рд╢рд┐рдерд┐рд▓ рд╣реЛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рди) рдирд╣реАрдВ (рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерддреН) рд╢рд┐рдерд┐рд▓ рд╣реЛ рд╡рд╛ (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗ) рджрд╛рд╣рд┐рдиреЗ (рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗ) рд╣рд╛рде рдореЗрдВ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдорд▓рдХ рдзрд░реЗрдВ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд░рд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдореИрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЛ (рджрдзреЗ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реВрдБ рд╡рд╛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ) рд╕рдм (рдЗрд╖реБрдзреНрдпрддреЗ) рдзрдиреБрд╖реН рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЬрдирд╕рдореВрд╣ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рддреВрдБ (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рджреЗрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рдХрд╛ (рдЖ, рдКрд╣рд┐рд╖реЗ) рддрд░реНрдХ-рд╡рд┐рддрд░реНрдХ рдХрд░рддрд╛ (рдЗрддреН) рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рдЬреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ) рд╕рдм (рд╕реБрдХреГрддреЗ) рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬрдирд╕рдореВрд╣ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╡рд╣ рд╕реБрдЦ (рдЗрддреН) рд╣реА рдХреЗ (рд╡рд╛рд░рдореН) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐, рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рд╕рдм рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрдд рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рдХрд░ рд╕рдмрдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╕рдм рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рджреЛрд╖реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд░рд╣рд┐рдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдХрд░ рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╛ рдЕрд░рддрд┐рд╕реНрддрд░рдгрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╕реБрдГ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдпрд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрди рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерджрд┐рд╡ рди рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерджреНрджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗ рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗ рдЖрдорд▓рдХрдЗрд╡ рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджрдзреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд╛ рдЗрд╖реБрдзреНрдпрддреЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореЛрд╣рд┐рд╖реЗ рддрдереЗрджреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ рд╕реБрдХреГрддреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐ рд╕ рд╕реБрдЦрдорд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдВ рд╡реНрдпреГрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ) рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдГ (рдЕрд░рддрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрдГ (рд╡рд╕реБрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдердордХрд▓реНрдкрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдГ (рджрдзреЗ) рдзрд░рд╛рдорд┐ (рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗ) (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗ) (рддрд░рдгрд┐рдГ) рддрд╛рд░рдХрдГ (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерддреН) рд╢реНрд░рдердпреЗрддреН (рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдпрд╛) рдЖрддреНрдордирдГ рд╢реНрд░рд╡ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдерддреН) рд╢реНрд░рдердпреЗрддреНред рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрднрдпрддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рдбрднрд╛рд╡рдГред (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдЗрд╖реБрдзреНрдпрддреЗ) рдЗрд╖реБрдз рдЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд░рд╛) рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рджрд╛рддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рдореН (рдЖ) (рдКрд╣рд┐рд╖реЗ) рд╡рд┐рддрд░реНрдХрдпрд╕рд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИ) (рдЗрддреН) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реБрдХреГрддреЗ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреЗ (рд╡рд╛рд░рдореН) рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреБрдореН (рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд┐рд╡ (рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛) рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд╜рд░реНрдереЗ (рдЛрдгреНрд╡рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni is a most amiable friend in human infirmity through the means of sacrifices; the beloved protector of all in sacrifices, like a victorious prince, he alights upon the oblations of men when plural ced upon the altar; he preserves us from the malignity of Varuс╣Зa; from the malignity of the mighty deity (of sin).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tr─Бsate varuс╣Зasya dh┼лrter maho devasya dh┼лrteс╕е, preserves us from the malevolence of the obstructor of religious rites (varuс╣Зa = v─Бraka, the impeder)– from the malevolence of the mighty deity presiding over sin, p─Бpa-devat─Б

Jamison Brereton

He has been established as most beneficial in the ritual enclosure belonging to Manu; Agni (has been established) like a noble clanlord at the sacrificesтАФa dear clanlord at the sacrifices.
He is master of the oblations of the sons of Manu, the oblations
prepared with the refreshing drink.
He will rescue us from the injury of Varuс╣ЗaтАФfrom the injury of the great god.

Jamison Brereton Notes

j├йnya- is of unclear formation (see EWA s.v.), and opinion is generally split between a derivation from тИЪjan тАШbe bornтАЩ (e.g., Grassmann тАШedelтАЩ) and тИЪji тАШwinтАЩ (e.g., Witzel Got┼Н тАШsiegreichтАЩ), with EWA tentatively opting for the latter. In contrast, I find that a meaning тАШnobleтАЩ vel sim. better fits most passages and consider it a pseudo-gerundive to тИЪjan, built to the zero-grade formant j─Б- (cf. in this hymn j─Бyata 1a, ├бj─Бyata 4f, g), with the semantic development тАШ(worthy) to be born, noble, thoroughbredтАЩ; its use with inanimate v├бsu (e.g., the cmpd. jeny─Б-vasu- тАШhaving noble goodsтАЩ) is simply an extension comparable to English тАЬnoble metalsтАЭ (vs. base metals).

Griffith

That Agni hath been set most kind in camp of men, in sacrifice like a Lord victorious, like a dear Lord in sacred rites.
His are the oblations of mankind when offered up at Ila’s place.
He shall preserve us from Varuna’s chastisement, yea, from the great God’s chastisement.

Oldenberg

He has been established as the most blissful one in the enclosures of men, Agni, at the sacrifices, like a noble lord of the clans, a beloved lord of the clans at the sacrifices: he rules over the oblations of men to which nourishing power has been imparted 1. May he protect us from harm that comes from Varuna, from harm 2 that comes from the great god.

Geldner

Agni ist als der am meisten Frommende ├╝ber den menschlichen Opferbund, ├╝ber die Opfer gesetzt wie ein stammverwandter Clanherr, ├╝ber die Opfer als der liebe Clanherr. Er verf├╝gt ├╝ber die Opferspenden der Menschen, die von der Id bereitet sind. Er m├╢ge uns vor Varuna┬┤s T├╝cke bewahren, vor der T├╝cke des gro├Яen Gottes.

Grassmann

Als bester ist im Menschenstamm er eingesetzt, bei Opfern Agni als der edle Hausesherr bei Opfern als der liebe Herr; Sein sind der Menschen Opfer all’, die andachtsvoll ergossen sind; Er m├╢g’ uns sch├╝tzen vor der Strafe Varuna’s, des grossen Gottes Strafe uns.

Elizarenkova

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡реЗ рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ) рддреГрдкреНрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡рд╣ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдзреВрд░реНрддреНрддреЗрдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХ рд╕реЗ (рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕рддреЗ) рд╡реЗрдорди рдХрд░рд╛рддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рдзреВрд░реНрддреНрддреЗрдГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЛ рдирд╛рд╢рдиреЗ рдФрд░ (рдорд╣рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдкрд╛рд╕ рд╕реЗ рдЬреЛ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╖реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдЗрд│рд╛) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдХреГрддрд╛рдирд┐) рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╢реБрджреНрдз рд╡рдЪрди (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛) рдЬреЛ рдХрд┐ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрдВ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рддрдерд╛ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ рд╕рдмрдХреЛ (рдкрддреНрдпрддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╖реБ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд╛ (рдЬреЗрдиреНрдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реЗ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рд╡реГрдЬрдиреЗ) рдЙрд╕ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рдЧрдорди рдХрд░рддреЗ (рд╣рд┐рддрдГ) рд╣рд┐рдд рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╢рдВрддрдордГ) рдЕрддреАрд╡ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░реА рд╣реЛрддрд╛ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдзрд░реНрдо рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рддреЗ, рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреЗ, рдбрд╛рдБрдХреВ рдЖрджрд┐ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЬреЛ рдбрд░ рдЙрд╕рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдЬрди рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рдЕрдиреНрдзрдкрд░рдореНрдкрд░рд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдХреБрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдХреЗ рд░реЛрдХрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey, (the devout), praise Agni, the invoker (of the gods), the possessor of wealth, the beloved, the thoughtful; they have recourse to him as to a sovereign; they have recourse to him as the bearer of oblations; to him, who is the life (of all living beings), who knows all things, the offerer of oblations, the object of worship, the sage; the sacred (priests), desirous of affluence, murmur (his praises) to obtain his protection; desirous of affluence, they murmur (his praises) in their hymns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, the Hotar, the depository of goods do they reverently invoke; the dear, most conspicuous one they have installed as the spoked wheel
(of the sacrifice)тАФthey have installed as the conveyor of oblationsтАФ the one who provides all lifetimes and all possessions, the Hotar
deserving the sacrifice, the sage poet.
The gods, seeking goods, (have installed) the lusty one, for helpтАФseeking goods (they have installed) the lusty one with hymns.

Griffith

Agni the Priest they supplicate to grant them wealth: him, dear, most thoughtful, have they made their messenger, him, offering-bearer have they made,
Beloved of all, who knoweth all, the Priest, the Holy one, the Sage–
Him, Friend, for help, the Gods when they are fain for wealth, him, Friend, with hymns, when fain for wealth.

Oldenberg

They magnify Agni the Hotri, the dispenser of goods. They have roused the beloved, the most shining steward 1 (of sacrifice); they have roused the carrier of oblations. The gods desirous of goods (have roused) him in whom all life dwells, who possesses all wealth, the Hotri, the worshipful sage, the lovely one for the sake of bliss; with praises (they have roused), desirous of goods, the lovely one.

Geldner

Den Agni berufen sie zum Hotri, den Sch├дtzeberger. Den lieben ausgezeichneten haben sie als Wagenlenker angestellt, als lebensl├дnglichen Hotri den allwissenden, den opferw├╝rdigen Seher, die G├╢tter den Erfreulichen zum Schutz, Gutes w├╝nschend, unter Lobreden den Erfreulichen, Gutes w├╝nschend.

Grassmann

Den Priester Agni flehn sie an um Schatzgewinn, sie haben ihn als lieben kl├╝gsten Opferer, als Opferfahrer eingesetzt; Als weisen, hehren Priester ihn, der alles Gut und Leben hegt, Als Freund die G├╢tter gutbegehrend zum Genuss, als Freund die S├дnger voll Begier.

Elizarenkova
